  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7c7beb1c-ead9-4b48-8f2d-b13fbb3a0e21'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer16846412628362750236">A catastrophic, unexplainable plane crash leaves three hundred and thirty dead--no survivors. Among the victims are the wife and two daughters of Joe Carpenter, a Los Angeles Post crime reporter. <br/>A year after the crash, still gripped by an almost paralyzing grief, Joe encounters a woman named Rose, who claims to have survived the crash. She holds out the possibility of a s</span>
  <span id="freeText16846412628362750236" style="display:none">A catastrophic, unexplainable plane crash leaves three hundred and thirty dead--no survivors. Among the victims are the wife and two daughters of Joe Carpenter, a Los Angeles Post crime reporter. <br />A year after the crash, still gripped by an almost paralyzing grief, Joe encounters a woman named Rose, who claims to have survived the crash. She holds out the possibility of a secret that will bring Joe peace of mind. But before he can ask any questions, she slips away. <br />Driven now by rage (have the authorities withheld information?) and a hope almost as unbearable as his grief (if there is one survivor, are there others?), Joe sets out to find the mysterious woman. His search immediately leads him into the path of a powerful and shadowy organization hell-bent on stopping Rose before she can reveal what she knows about the crash. <br />Sole Survivor unfolds at a heart-stopping pace, as a desperate chase and a shattering emotional odyssey lead Joe to a truth that will force him to reassess everything he thought he knew about life and death--a truth that, given the chance, will rock the world and redefine the destiny of humanity.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16846412628362750236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1421853971" />
    <a title="Quentin Wallace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33274222-quentin-wallace"><img alt="Quentin Wallace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595984858p2/33274222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1421853971?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Quentin Wallace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Quentin Wallace" href="/user/show/33274222-quentin-wallace">Quentin Wallace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6512382-sole-survivor">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1421853971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10108037102610177519">This book to me was a mixed bag. On one hand, it was a pretty cool story, and the action near the end was very suspenseful and engaging. However, I also think the book could have been shorter and been much better. I find many books have an issue of just being too long which causes the story to drag. Perhaps it's just me, I'm not sure.<br/><br/>This story was very emotional and was a character study as well as a suspense story. I will admit I had guessed at least part of the big reveal, although not exactl</span>
  <span id="freeText10108037102610177519" style="display:none">This book to me was a mixed bag. On one hand, it was a pretty cool story, and the action near the end was very suspenseful and engaging. However, I also think the book could have been shorter and been much better. I find many books have an issue of just being too long which causes the story to drag. Perhaps it's just me, I'm not sure.<br /><br />This story was very emotional and was a character study as well as a suspense story. I will admit I had guessed at least part of the big reveal, although not exactly and not every part of it. Overall I found it to be like most Koontz books, in that they are good but never quite reach great. I'm still a fan, he just never quite reaches that top level for me. Then again, I haven't read that many Koontz books, so as I read more I may find some I like more than what I've read so far.<br /><br />Now, one thing that did bother me with this book was the writing style. There was no traditional dialogue. It was all written with no quotations like someone was telling you what everyone said rather than the person actually speaking. It's not as confusing as it sounds, but it did take me out of the story slightly.<br /><br />Overall this was a good book that could have been great with some edits. I did enjoy it, and would recommend it to suspense fans.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10108037102610177519" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3462079266" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3462079266" />
    <a title="Ange H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21166492-ange-h"><img alt="Ange H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509888949p2/21166492.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3462079266?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ange H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ange H" href="/user/show/21166492-ange-h">Ange H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780679425267" href="/book/show/666760.Sole_Survivor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21166492-ange-h?shelf=real-books-i-own">real-books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3462079266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7096691905904466734">After not reading any of Dean Koontz particular brand of bizarre for quite a while, I probably appreciated this story more than I otherwise might have. A mystery woman walks away from a devastating plane crash, and then begins to contact the loved ones of the victims. After her visits, these people commit suicide in horrific ways. Meanwhile, very powerful people are trying to find this woman and stop her.<br/><br/>I don’t think it’s one of his better ones, but you kind of can’t stop reading until you find</span>
  <span id="freeText7096691905904466734" style="display:none">After not reading any of Dean Koontz particular brand of bizarre for quite a while, I probably appreciated this story more than I otherwise might have. A mystery woman walks away from a devastating plane crash, and then begins to contact the loved ones of the victims. After her visits, these people commit suicide in horrific ways. Meanwhile, very powerful people are trying to find this woman and stop her.<br /><br />I don’t think it’s one of his better ones, but you kind of can’t stop reading until you find out what’s going on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7096691905904466734" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1421514056" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1421514056" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4041033-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476116592p2/4041033.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1421514056?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/4041033-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1421514056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1323600892148812554">Reviewed first at <a href='http://brunnersbookshelf.blogspot.com/2015/11/soul-survivor-by-dean-koontz.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Brunner's Bookshelf</a><br/><br/>I have to say that I am not a huge Dean Koontz fan. My wife was with his earlier work but there came a point when his books just got really weird and our interest faded. I have some of his books that I really liked, Tick Tock and Life Expectancy to name a few. This was another book that kept popping up in my hunt for horro books for the R.I.P. challenge. I figured I would give it a try. Let's just say I was expecting a horror novel and this isn't.<br/><br/>The book is </span>
  <span id="freeText1323600892148812554" style="display:none">Reviewed first at <a href="http://brunnersbookshelf.blogspot.com/2015/11/soul-survivor-by-dean-koontz.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Brunner's Bookshelf</a><br /><br />I have to say that I am not a huge Dean Koontz fan. My wife was with his earlier work but there came a point when his books just got really weird and our interest faded. I have some of his books that I really liked, Tick Tock and Life Expectancy to name a few. This was another book that kept popping up in my hunt for horro books for the R.I.P. challenge. I figured I would give it a try. Let's just say I was expecting a horror novel and this isn't.<br /><br />The book is all about a man who is suffering after the loss of his wife and two daughters in a plane crash. Wanting to die he goes to visit the graves one last time. When he arrives he finds a strange woman taking pictures of the headstones and FBI types following him. This opens the book up to what could have been a really interesting suspense thriller. Sadly about half way through the book my interest tanked. I couldn't keep focused and my mind kept wandering. I was mechanically reading just to get through this. It also seemed about this point that the story was just all over the place. My lack of focus might have had something to do with this but I'm not sure. I will own up when my dislike of a book is my own doing but I really tried to like this. <br /><br />By the end of this book I was so happy to be finished with this. I felt the ending was terrible. It felt like the book started out to be one thing and Koontz forgot how he started the story so it ended as if it was a different story. I was really disappointed. This started out with so much potential and then just lost me. It's over and I can move on. I give this 2 out of 5 stars and really it was more like 1.5 stars. I also had every intention in including this in my R.I.P. challenge but I'm going to skip it. I have already had enough books to complete the challenge more than two times and this is not what I was expecting being at the top of several horror fiction lists. So I decided to save this review till after the challenge and just focus on my Halloween week posts. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1323600892148812554" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1397542153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2772662914782152141">Made it through 30% before I finally gave it up. I've only read a few Koontz books and wasn't impressed by what I did read. Sole Survivor only confirms that I'm not a Koontz fan.<br/><br/>You'd think it would be pretty difficult to make a man who lost his wife and two daughters in a plane crash unsympathetic, but Koontz makes it look easy. The first 20% of the book is the main character going on and on and on about he's suffering, miserable, angry, unable to ever move on, yadda yadda yadda. We get it. The</span>
  <span id="freeText2772662914782152141" style="display:none">Made it through 30% before I finally gave it up. I've only read a few Koontz books and wasn't impressed by what I did read. Sole Survivor only confirms that I'm not a Koontz fan.<br /><br />You'd think it would be pretty difficult to make a man who lost his wife and two daughters in a plane crash unsympathetic, but Koontz makes it look easy. The first 20% of the book is the main character going on and on and on about he's suffering, miserable, angry, unable to ever move on, yadda yadda yadda. We get it. The main character is in a bad place. Can we start the story now? <br /><br />Unfortunately, the annoying main character isn't the only problem. I'm not sure if Koontz was trying to stretch his literary wings, but Sole Survivor is filled with over the top prose and endless descriptions that seemed to have been written to establish Koontz's literary cred. Bleagh. If I want boring literary descriptions, I'll check out the Booker Prize nominees. <br /><br />I ultimately read spoilers about the rest of the plot. Frankly, it sounded nonsensical so I'm glad I checked out. </span>

The change had begun the previous day, when he'd gone to the cemetery. Ever since, a shift seemed to be progressing with gathering power and speed, as though the world of Einsteinian laws had intersected with a universe where the rules of energy and matter were so different as to baffle the wisest mathematicians and the proudest physicists.<br /><br />This new reality was both more piercingly beautiful and more fearsome than the one that it replaced. He knew the change was subjective and would never reverse itself. Nothing this side of death would ever again seem simple to him; the smoothest surface hid unknowable depths and complexities. <br />______<br /><br />. . . the white trunks of the paper birches glowed like painted doorjambs, the deeply moody shadows between like open doors to futures best left unvisited. <br />______<br /><br /></i></span>

<div id="review_1075896315" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1075896315" />
    <a title="Steve Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15445898-steve-lee"><img alt="Steve Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1355397124p2/15445898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1075896315?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve Lee" href="/user/show/15445898-steve-lee">Steve Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1075896315" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9982956026913014825">Perhaps it is just me, but this book ultimately seemed to be little more than the preaching and proselytising of a religious fundamentalist. At one stage in the book, a prominent biologist even goes to lengths to condemn evolution in the manner that only a creationist lunatic would. It was almost like reading the AIG website or a Jehovah Witness Watchtower pamphlet. <br/><br/>I am currently reading another of his novels (The Taking) and find that this, too, is interjected with out-of-place statements and </span>
  <span id="freeText9982956026913014825" style="display:none">Perhaps it is just me, but this book ultimately seemed to be little more than the preaching and proselytising of a religious fundamentalist. At one stage in the book, a prominent biologist even goes to lengths to condemn evolution in the manner that only a creationist lunatic would. It was almost like reading the AIG website or a Jehovah Witness Watchtower pamphlet. <br /><br />I am currently reading another of his novels (The Taking) and find that this, too, is interjected with out-of-place statements and claims that one would only find spew from the mouth of a fundamentalist Christian or Muslim. <br /><br />And while this shouldn't matter (after all, where would such things be better suited than in a work of fiction?) it is so out of place with the actual story, and has little to no relevance to it, that it detracts from the story itself. While Sole Survivor is ultimately a religious message, there was no need nor relevance in attempting to dismiss evolution or erroneously claiming that most scientists have come to realise it isn't true and that science is continually 'proving' the fact of intelligent design, to get that message across. <br /><br />It would not in the least surprise me if the next book of his I read contains the claim that scientists have demonstrated that humans and dinosaurs lived together, the world is only 6,000 years old or that the Noah's Ark fiction actually happened. All of these stupidities would in themselves be entirely acceptable IF they were relevant part of the fictional novel itself. But when pointlessly and irrelevantly included, it becomes rather off-putting. The only thing I shall remember this novel for is its creationist-style ignorance of science.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9982956026913014825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3084979551" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3659710952516126344">I’m a big Dean Koontz fan, I’m always eager to dive into his book, and I’ve slowly been working my way through his backlist. Although I have found a few books I haven’t loved, I’ve enjoyed the majority. With Sole Survivor, we have a book where my rating sits in the middle.<br/><br/>At first, I was intrigued by this one. There were many aspects I was curious about, details that had me hooked. I was happy to power through it, turning the pages at a rapid pace. However, I did find this one dragged a bit at t</span>
  <span id="freeText3659710952516126344" style="display:none">I’m a big Dean Koontz fan, I’m always eager to dive into his book, and I’ve slowly been working my way through his backlist. Although I have found a few books I haven’t loved, I’ve enjoyed the majority. With Sole Survivor, we have a book where my rating sits in the middle.<br /><br />At first, I was intrigued by this one. There were many aspects I was curious about, details that had me hooked. I was happy to power through it, turning the pages at a rapid pace. However, I did find this one dragged a bit at times. There were certain details I would have liked to see more of, certain aspects that were never given the depth I would have liked, and the ending left me wishing there had been a bit more.<br /><br />All in all, there were some good ideas with this one, but it was not done as well as other Koontz book. It’s worth a read if you’re a Koontz fan, but I would not recommend it as an introduction to his work.</span>

<div id="review_131477841" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/131477841" />
    <a title="Johnny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3784000-johnny"><img alt="Johnny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545250646p2/3784000.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/131477841?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johnny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johnny" href="/user/show/3784000-johnny">Johnny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780747254348" href="/book/show/959366.Sole_Survivor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3784000-johnny?shelf=own-it">own-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer131477841&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer131477841" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6248221197725338636">One year after a plane crash took away his wife and two daughters, Joe Carpenter meets a woman who was supposed to have died in that accident as well, holding the secret of what really happened.<br/>	<br/>The title “Sole Survivor” doesn’t only point at this woman, but also at Joe himself. He’s the one left behind, the only one of his family still alive. The book is about loss, about grieving, accepting death, and about faith, believing that the human soul doesn’t just vanish into nothingness when shed of </span>
  <span id="freeText6248221197725338636" style="display:none">One year after a plane crash took away his wife and two daughters, Joe Carpenter meets a woman who was supposed to have died in that accident as well, holding the secret of what really happened.<br />	<br />The title “Sole Survivor” doesn’t only point at this woman, but also at Joe himself. He’s the one left behind, the only one of his family still alive. The book is about loss, about grieving, accepting death, and about faith, believing that the human soul doesn’t just vanish into nothingness when shed of its mortal coils.<br />	<br />All this makes it quite heavy to swallow. It’s a dark story, a sad story, a <br />depressing story even. Joe is a man who has basically given up on life and is just waiting to die, too scared to take care of it himself. And if it weren’t for a chance encounter on a public beach at the beginning of the novel, he might have gotten his wish. There’s almost no siganture Koontz humor in this novel. It’s a very serious story.<br />	<br />“Sole Survivor” is mostly a mystery story, a conspiracy story, of the sort where the answers stay away until the final act. When they are delivered, the style changes very much and it’s like we’ve suddenly been transported into a science fiction story. Until we reach that conclusion, however, we’re pulled along with Joe into a very compelling investigation. But Joe isn’t just riding shotgun; he sets things in motion as well, even though he has no clue what’s going on.<br />	<br />Even though the novel features an enigmatic woman, there’s no trace of a love story here. The book vows to transcent material and physical love and instead concentrates on the bigger picture.<br />	<br />While not necessarily religious in nature, it does discuss some of the building blocks of religious groups, combined with some radical sciences – which is in fact the only thing that makes it recognizably a Koontz novel. It’s a first taste of things to come in “From the Corner of His Eye”, but also the Chris Snow books, as if Koontz is testing the waters with some variety of his theories, to see whether his audience is open enough for them.<br />	<br />Plotwise, “Sole Survivor” always reminds me of “The Eyes of Darkness”, <br />while the ending comes closer to “Dark Rivers of the Heart”. It’s a story that doesn’t really end, because it creates some kind of alternate universe of our world where the villains have become too large to be dismissed.<br />	<br />I remember when I first read this book, I was so totally swept away by the ending, and I was ready to believe in it myself. I didn’t go so far as to actually take snapshots of gravestones, but I think I did stare at a photo of a loved one passed on, somewhat in the same way as I sat at a kitchen table staring at a salt shaker after reading “Strangers” for the first time. Reading the book again now, the impact is gone. Not because I believe less, but because the idea is no longer original, because I’ve encountered it – or a variety of it – in so many other books since.<br />	<br />In the finale, I thought that Joe would reach out for the boy, tell him he cared and wanted to help him, convince him to stop the attack and perhaps break him out of the facility in true “The Eyes of Darkness” style. The ending in the woods also reminded me of this movie “Fallen” with Denzel Washington.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6248221197725338636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_159144516" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159144516" />
    <a title="Karen B." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5230033-karen-b"><img alt="Karen B." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308784537p2/5230033.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159144516?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen B." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen B." href="/user/show/5230033-karen-b">Karen B.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5230033-karen-b?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5230033-karen-b?shelf=koontz">koontz</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5230033-karen-b?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159144516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4543754295973004110">Koontz has a nice blend of characterization and plot in this novel. We meet Joe Carpenter who has basically given up on life after the death of his family in a plane crash a year ago. He seems to have nothing to live for. Then he meets a strange woman at the graveside of his wife and daughters taking photos of the gravestones. Why? Then he finds that she is being chased and he is under being watched as well. Why again? The reporter in him is still alive as he becomes determined to find out what </span>
  <span id="freeText4543754295973004110" style="display:none">Koontz has a nice blend of characterization and plot in this novel. We meet Joe Carpenter who has basically given up on life after the death of his family in a plane crash a year ago. He seems to have nothing to live for. Then he meets a strange woman at the graveside of his wife and daughters taking photos of the gravestones. Why? Then he finds that she is being chased and he is under being watched as well. Why again? The reporter in him is still alive as he becomes determined to find out what is going on. Is Rose really a survivor of the plane crash? Is there more to the plane crash than what he has learned so far? How is Rose tied to his children? Joe begins his own investigation, running from the same forces that are after Rose. Is it possible that his daughter, Nina, is alive? Is there such a thing as an afterlife? Koontz once again leads us on a fascinating journey through Joe's search for the truth.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4543754295973004110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2763719-john?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer486376457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17837502448033973985">Definitely on the short list of Koontz's best work, SOLE SURVIVOR is a wildly entertaining thriller with surprisingly ambitious emotional and spiritual underpinnings. Not only does it contain one of the most powerful hooks I've ever come across, but, in between scenes of grisly murders and exciting chases, Koontz aims to teach readers a little something about life. For a suspense novel, however, it all feels a bit overwritten. Koontz tries to imbibe SOLE SURVIVOR with the trappings of "serious l</span>
  <span id="freeText17837502448033973985" style="display:none">Definitely on the short list of Koontz's best work, SOLE SURVIVOR is a wildly entertaining thriller with surprisingly ambitious emotional and spiritual underpinnings. Not only does it contain one of the most powerful hooks I've ever come across, but, in between scenes of grisly murders and exciting chases, Koontz aims to teach readers a little something about life. For a suspense novel, however, it all feels a bit overwritten. Koontz tries to imbibe SOLE SURVIVOR with the trappings of "serious literature" but doesn't pull it off 100% effectively. As a result, Koontz's too-frequent use of complicated metaphors eventually becomes distracting, though he certainly does an amazing job at being descriptive. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17837502448033973985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2269587951" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12555429141353309747">3.75 stars.<br/> This is my first Dean Koontz novel so I didn't know what to expect. Upon finishing the book it was like reading Stephen King crossed with Harlen Coben, with a sprinkle of Michael Chrichton added for good measure.<br/> <br/> Reading the synopsis made this sound like your typical thriller novel. A shocking revelation, a character un-equip to deal with what is thrown at him. You expect lots of plot twists and an ending you couldn't predict if you had fifty guesses. You got most of this, but what </span>
  <span id="freeText12555429141353309747" style="display:none">3.75 stars.<br /> This is my first Dean Koontz novel so I didn't know what to expect. Upon finishing the book it was like reading Stephen King crossed with Harlen Coben, with a sprinkle of Michael Chrichton added for good measure.<br /> <br /> Reading the synopsis made this sound like your typical thriller novel. A shocking revelation, a character un-equip to deal with what is thrown at him. You expect lots of plot twists and an ending you couldn't predict if you had fifty guesses. You got most of this, but what made this different to other thrillers that I've read is the amount of detail in Koontz's descriptions. His use of language was also much richer than is usually standard in this kind of book. Whether this is something that entices or puts you off depends on your personal taste.<br /><br /> Answers were slow to materialise. I was less than eighty pages (approximately) to the end and wondering if I'd actually be told what was the cause of everything. When they came they shocked me. Not because it was so horrific, but because they came from so left field. Am element I would never have imagined being introduced really through me for a loop. It made for an interesting end to the story but I wonder how others felt / will feel about it.<br /> <br /> This was on par for being a 4 star book. And then the final chapter happened. It wasn't refereed to as it, but it was pretty much the epilogue. Given what had occurred and the reasoning that events had played out, it made little sense to me why all of a sudden everything was deemed to be resolved. I can't go into details because I don't want to include spoilers but why something that had happened only a few pages previously couldn't be repeated with ease made no sense.<br /> And then the last page and a half. I'm sure it was meant as a summary but it came across as preachy. Having just read a book that did little more than preach I'm happy for this type of narrative to be left out of fictional writing</span>
  <a data-text-id="12555429141353309747" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2373919012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6540054233575880331">Time taken to read - 3 days<br/><br/>Pages - 403<br/><br/>Publisher - Bantam Books<br/><br/>Source - The Works<br/><br/>Blurb from Goodreads <br/><br/>A catastrophic, unexplainable plane crash leaves three hundred and thirty dead--no survivors. Among the victims are the wife and two daughters of Joe Carpenter, a Los Angeles Post crime reporter. <br/>A year after the crash, still gripped by an almost paralyzing grief, Joe encounters a woman named Rose, who claims to have survived the crash. She holds out the possibility of a secret that will bring Jo</span>
  <span id="freeText6540054233575880331" style="display:none">Time taken to read - 3 days<br /><br />Pages - 403<br /><br />Publisher - Bantam Books<br /><br />Source - The Works<br /><br />Blurb from Goodreads <br /><br />A catastrophic, unexplainable plane crash leaves three hundred and thirty dead--no survivors. Among the victims are the wife and two daughters of Joe Carpenter, a Los Angeles Post crime reporter. <br />A year after the crash, still gripped by an almost paralyzing grief, Joe encounters a woman named Rose, who claims to have survived the crash. She holds out the possibility of a secret that will bring Joe peace of mind. But before he can ask any questions, she slips away. <br />Driven now by rage (have the authorities withheld information?) and a hope almost as unbearable as his grief (if there is one survivor, are there others?), Joe sets out to find the mysterious woman. His search immediately leads him into the path of a powerful and shadowy organization hell-bent on stopping Rose before she can reveal what she knows about the crash. <br />Sole Survivor unfolds at a heart-stopping pace, as a desperate chase and a shattering emotional odyssey lead Joe to a truth that will force him to reassess everything he thought he knew about life and death--a truth that, given the chance, will rock the world and redefine the destiny of humanity.<br /><br /><br /><br />My Review<br /><br />The one year anniversary since his wife and children's plane crashed and Joe is no closer to getting over his grief. When he happens upon the mysterious Rose, taking photographs of his loved ones grave then witnessing her being attacked, curiosity is piqued. Joe embarks on a journey to find out who she is, what she knows about his family and who then men are that have been following him.<br /><br />I would say this book, for me, split into two stories. The first is all about Joe, grief, the relatives of those on board the aircraft and of course the mysterious Rose. Joe finds she has visited other families who lost someone on the crash and what befell them after her contact. The second part of the story we find out all about Rose, some mysterious happenings and the need to suspend belief a wee bit. There are so many parts I could talk about, humanity, what is right and wrong, ethics however to do so would go into spoilers, something I refuse to do. Would love to gab ideas though with folk who have read it, in a private forum or gabbing so as not to spoil it for anyone else. Certainly interesting ideas and sure conspiracy fans would love it and suggest stuff like that already happens somewhere in the world.<br /><br />Interesting, different and certainly I wanted to find out what was coming next. Read Koontz before and will read him again, I like this I just didn't love it. I also preferred the first half of the book I think, 3 out of 5 for me this time.<br /><br /></span>

        <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction">Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129251152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3158531834641063810">Joe Carpenter is a man paralyzed by grief and anger. On the one year anniversary of the plane crash that killed his beloved wife and daughters he visits their cemetery and spots a woman taking pictures of their grave marker. He approaches her and sets off a series of events that make him question if the death of his family and 300 others was the intentional work of officials attempting to cover up something that could possibly change mankind for all time. As he digs for the truth he witnesses an</span>
  <span id="freeText3158531834641063810" style="display:none">Joe Carpenter is a man paralyzed by grief and anger. On the one year anniversary of the plane crash that killed his beloved wife and daughters he visits their cemetery and spots a woman taking pictures of their grave marker. He approaches her and sets off a series of events that make him question if the death of his family and 300 others was the intentional work of officials attempting to cover up something that could possibly change mankind for all time. As he digs for the truth he witnesses and discovers strange, terrifying, incomprehensible events, and finds evidence that is impossible for him to ignore. He finds a purpose for living once he realizes he may be the only person left alive to expose the truth.<br /><br />Dean Koontz usually writes so much more than an eerie, suspense filled page-turner and SOLE SURVIVOR is no exception. He creates characters who are human, people you care about and anguish with, everyday people stuck in extraordinary situations. He's outdone himself with the character of Joe. Poor, tortured Joe. His grief is expressed so vividly I felt his sorrow and my heart broke about a million times as he's reminded of his wife and girls in nearly every thing he does.<br /><br />Any book that can keep me on edge like this one did and make me care so much about a character gets my recommendation. There were a few parts that dragged a little bit but overall it was an interesting, emotional and nail-biting read.<br /><br />Koontz writes an thrilling story and he continually surprises me but it's his talent for characterization that keeps him on the top of my favorite author list. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3158531834641063810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2530222909591686060">I discovered once I got into this book that I remembered the movie based on it (very loosely based). My daughter tells me I actually tried to read it once before and laid it aside.<br/><br/>I can sort of see why.<br/><br/>For a long, long (long,long,long,long) time this book does try the patience.   <span id="freeText2530222909591686060" style="display:none">I discovered once I got into this book that I remembered the movie based on it (very loosely based). My daughter tells me I actually tried to read it once before and laid it aside.<br /><br />I can sort of see why.<br /><br />For a long, long (long,long,long,long) time this book does try the patience. Our protagonist is in despair over the sudden loss of his family in a plane crash. The event is a year in the past but Joe Carpenter is still shattered. <br /><br />And he tells us about it...he loses control, he creeps out strangers by stopping them when he thinks they are his lost wife and daughter...and he goes on and on (and on, and on, and on, and on,) about it all.<br /><br />I really had to hold on tight to stay with the book.<br /><br />There's another thing...the idea here, Koontz has done it elsewhere, and better. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[A child brings spiritual enlightenment <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Let me suggest that you try <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15746.One_Door_Away_from_Heaven" title="One Door Away from Heaven by Dean Koontz" rel="nofollow noopener">One Door Away from Heaven</a> it's a far superior book and has the same basic plot idea at it's base. This one is okay...readable, not nearly Koontz's worst. It's just not all that great.<br /><br />My opinion of course. </span>

<div id="review_77440952" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77440952" />
    <a title="Natalie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2439366-natalie"><img alt="Natalie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1284990646p2/2439366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77440952?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie" href="/user/show/2439366-natalie">Natalie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77440952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10407115531481382544">I can't quite put my finger on what turned me off to this book. I think it's probably how depressing most of it is. The main character has lost his wife and both his children in a plane crash. This horrible experience is even worse for him because of the fact that he lost all belief in God as a young man. For most of the book, we experience his adventures from the point of view of a grieving husband and father without the comfort of a knowledge of what comes after this life. The strange experien</span>
  <span id="freeText10407115531481382544" style="display:none">I can't quite put my finger on what turned me off to this book. I think it's probably how depressing most of it is. The main character has lost his wife and both his children in a plane crash. This horrible experience is even worse for him because of the fact that he lost all belief in God as a young man. For most of the book, we experience his adventures from the point of view of a grieving husband and father without the comfort of a knowledge of what comes after this life. The strange experiences he suddenly is exposed to on the one year anniversary of the crash are long, drawn out, and very confusing for most of the book. We only get some idea of what's really going on very near the end. There are too many times where the character is very close to figuring something out, only to have enlightenment snatched from him. <br /><br />Many of Koontz's characters are able to make the tone of his books positive because of the way they look at life and interact with the people around them. This main character is depressing through the entire book. The positive message of this book comes a little too late for my tastes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10407115531481382544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5u4KCcxANMwwVVKmTKYz4PandfeEF1uUHST9TnwwYAQaLhHZyPE9k9fTyQewdWKDKLpakOTL7Lv3hLSAF3micw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5E4vSJuCLjxiF6S3+3qs2pPVs1jZzC1IDdIA7fq9jL8YjjSYnzMnY4WRPxYHqf25TcicP7kQmmfnckkjkfROyA==')})
  }
//]]>
